  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_64c02fac-63d2-48ba-91b2-75e2fe279819'
      });

<a href="/questions/1094620-is-there-romance-in-this-book">is there romance in this book?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/26854688-rob-trans"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/26854688-rob-trans">Rob Trans</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
It depends on how you define romance. If you define it as one party cynically using another, then the answer is yes. 
</span>

<div id="review_1303248108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1303248108" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1303248108?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1303248108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5394675805345155449">For the plot description I shamelessly plagiarized the first two and a half sentences of the official book description. The Earth no longer rotates. Science rules the dayside of the globe. Magic rules the World of Night. Jack of Shadows was a thief whose magic was strongly connected with shadows. In other words, he could not do any magic in complete absence of them. He was caught in the beginning of the book and executed. Being a supernatural being he had several lives, just like an ordinary cat</span>
  <span id="freeText5394675805345155449" style="display:none">For the plot description I shamelessly plagiarized the first two and a half sentences of the official book description. The Earth no longer rotates. Science rules the dayside of the globe. Magic rules the World of Night. Jack of Shadows was a thief whose magic was strongly connected with shadows. In other words, he could not do any magic in complete absence of them. He was caught in the beginning of the book and executed. Being a supernatural being he had several lives, just like an ordinary cat. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463275556i/19101657.jpg" width="340" height="340" alt="Cat" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He came back and sought revenge. <br><br>I am a big fan of Zelazny. I keep saying that even his minor efforts deserve 3 stars. This looks like one of them. The beginning was quite good; it slowed down by about one third in the book, but still remain decent until the second half. At that point I had to ask myself, "Who the heck wrote this part and why did the Grand Master of science fiction and fantasy let him/her destroy his work???" The very end became quite good - probably the best part, but at that time it was way too late. <br><br>Add to this the fact that during the bad part of the book I stopped caring about Jack and his fate and you will understand why I gave one of my all-time favorite science fiction writers only 3 stars this time. It is still not a waste of time by any means, but please if you are not familiar with Zelazny do not start your acquaintance with him with this novel. It has excellent ideas, but the execution really lacked. <br><br>At this point I have to recycle the first image I used here to show my face when I finished this novel:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463275556i/19101657.jpg" width="340" height="340" alt="Cat" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Boy, was I grumpy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5394675805345155449" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76435141" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76435141" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76435141?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451135766" href="/book/show/1346120.Jack_of_Shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=cordwainer-vance-zelazny-and-esque">cordwainer-vance-zelazny-and-esque</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-hugo">award-nominee-hugo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=rogues-and-scoundrels">rogues-and-scoundrels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=betrayal-and-revenge">betrayal-and-revenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=multiple-award-nominee">multiple-award-nominee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=award-nominee-locus">award-nominee-locus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1970-1979">1970-1979</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=science-fantasy">science-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76435141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12608839806969075543">Roger Zelazny…One of the <b>Grandest Masters</b> of Science Fantasy has yet to disappoint me and <i>Jack of Shadows</i> is no exception. Along with Jack Vance (to whom this book was an homage), there is no author better at stuffing story into less than 200 pages. This <b>GEMtastic</b> example weighs in a svelte 142 pages and contains a full serving of juicy plot with zero filler fat. <br/><br/>Jack of Shadows takes place on a world that does not rotate and so half of the planet is always sun side and the other half of the pla</span>
  <span id="freeText12608839806969075543" style="display:none">Roger Zelazny…One of the <b>Grandest Masters</b> of Science Fantasy has yet to disappoint me and <i>Jack of Shadows</i> is no exception. Along with Jack Vance (to whom this book was an homage), there is no author better at stuffing story into less than 200 pages. This <b>GEMtastic</b> example weighs in a svelte 142 pages and contains a full serving of juicy plot with zero filler fat. <br /><br />Jack of Shadows takes place on a world that does not rotate and so half of the planet is always sun side and the other half of the planet is perpetual night. The sun side is similar to our world and is governed by science and natural law. The night side is a place of magic where supernatural entities reign supreme. In addition, and important to the story, daysiders have souls and only one life, whereas nightsiders are soulless and can be resurrected numerous times (though a finite number). <br /><br />Our title character is a thief, powerful wizard and a lord of the nightside though, even among his brethren, Jack is unusual. Most of the nightside lords have places of power where they are at the strongest (i.e. their realms which are like feudal estates). Jack has no one place of power but is strongest wherever he can create shadows. Inside shadow he has unmatched strength. <br /><br />At the beginning of the story, Jack is apprehended as a thief and decapitated by one of this rivals (OUCH!!). Years later (as resurrection is not immediate), Jack awakens in the Dung Pits of Glyve at the West Pole of the world and begins his quest for revenge against those who killed him. <br /><br />However, this is NOT a simple revenge piece set in an interesting SF world. Jack quest for revenge becomes the catalyst for events that will shake the foundations of the planet and lead either to a brand new world ….or the destruction of everything. I am not going to give away any spoilers so will just say that I “LOVED” the ending. It has an aspect to it that is left purposely ambiguous and I think adds to the mystery of the work. <br /><br />With one <b>critical exception</b>, this story has a very <i>“Dying Earth”</i> feel to it, which is intentional as Zelazny wrote this story as a tribute to Vance. For example, Jack of the Shadows, like Cugel the Clever and other <i>Dying Earth</i> rogues, is a thief and a magician. Like Cugel’s adventures, this story involves an extended journey in which Jack encounters the strange wonders of the world and the many interesting characters living in it. <br /><br />The one critical exception is that this is a dark, serious tale and the light-hearted whimsy that Jack brought to his <i>“Dying Earth”</i> stories is distinctly absent. By absent, I don’t want to imply that this is a bad thing, but I wanted to make sure you didn’t pick this up looking for a bag of feel good. <br /><br />Jack is REALLY not a nice person. He does very bad things during the course of this book, some of them down right despicable. He's selfish, lonely, angry, filled with bitterness and shows zero compassion for those who have wronged him. Despite that, Zelazny makes you understand Jack and provides not only a reason for his behavior, but also a very interesting moment of “redemption” at the end of the story. The redemption isn’t perfect, it’s messy and far from clear cut…but so is life and I was impressed with how Zelazny handled it. <br /><br />Again…all this in 142 pages. <br /><br />As I have said before about Vance’s work, Zelazny's talent for providing a rich background and interesting characters with and economy of words is something special and a sign of true mastery over prose craft. He does this in a variety of ways. One of them is to take a pivotal event that will occur over a significant period of time and lay it out in such a way that the impact is immediate and yet the power of the event is not diminished. Here is an example: <blockquote>
  <i> ‘So be it,’ he said. ‘Yet all that have described to you will come to pass, and you will be with me to witness it.’<br />‘No. I will have taken my life long before.’<br />‘I will bend your will, and you will love me.’<br />‘You will never touch me, body or will.’<br />‘You will sleep now,’ he said, ‘and when you awaken we will be coupled. You will struggle briefly and you will yield to me—first your body, then your will. You will lie passive for a time, then I will come to you again and yet again. After that, it will be you who come to me. Now you will sleep while I sacrifice [______] upon his Lord’s altar and cleanse this place of all things which displease me. Dream well. A new life awaits you.’<br />And he departed, and these things were done as he had said.</i>
</blockquote> In a paragraph, Zelazny provides a chilling account of the brutal subjugation, rape and brain washing of one character by another. <br /><br />Often, dark and dire situations in stories can be gratuitously dragged out FOREVER or else you will find characters fearing promised torments that never come to pass as event intervene to save the characters. Here, in 9 words (<i>“and these things were done as he had said”</i>), Zelazny both makes real the promised horror and closes the door on any reprieve. While lacking the tension that drawing out the process might bring, he injects a powerful image into the readers mind and then moves on with the story leaving the reader to fill in the cracks and catch up because the next evocative moment could occur (and probably will) in the next paragraph. I’m sure there are far better examples out there, but hopefully this helps somewhat in seeing the effective use of economy Zelazny brings to his works. <br /><br />I thought this was a terrific story with a wonderful backstory, some memorable characters and an interesting plot. Again, loved the ending. 4.0 stars. HIGHLY RECOMMENDED!!<br /><br />Nominee: Hugo Award for Best Novel<br />Nominee: Locus Award for Best SF Novel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12608839806969075543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10350151120054974550">One of Zelazny's standalones; a dark and finely-faceted jewel of a book.<br/><br/>(Oh, OK, fine. The world is fixed; the East Pole points ever towards the sun, and the eastern hemisphere is forever in daylight and ruled by science. The West Pole is in eternal darkness, and the Darkside is ruled by magic. In between, of course, is a narrow strip of twilight. Shadowjack is a thief (the greatest in all of the Darkside? well, certainly, he has an opinion on the subject) who draws power from shadows (as oppose</span>
  <span id="freeText10350151120054974550" style="display:none">One of Zelazny's standalones; a dark and finely-faceted jewel of a book.<br /><br />(Oh, OK, fine. The world is fixed; the East Pole points ever towards the sun, and the eastern hemisphere is forever in daylight and ruled by science. The West Pole is in eternal darkness, and the Darkside is ruled by magic. In between, of course, is a narrow strip of twilight. Shadowjack is a thief (the greatest in all of the Darkside? well, certainly, he has an opinion on the subject) who draws power from shadows (as opposed to the other Darkside lords, whose powers are geographically fixed). A potentially routine heist goes badly wrong, leaving Jack to make his way back from the West Pole through dangers untold and hardships unnumbered, his mind fixed upon revenge upon those who wronged him, a quest that will take him through the Twilight into the Dayside and back. The language is evocative and precise -- Zelazny freely owns that the book is his tribute to Jack Vance and is his [Zelazny's] attempt to emulate Vance's style. Certainly, he comes a whole lot closer than most ...)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12613721707177763285">Time to te-read some Roger Zelazny stuff. Though I re-read the Amber series periodically, I've been very lax about revisiting the other stuff of this top-tier fantastic author! 😯<br/><br/>Post Re-read: I remember reading this AGES ago, and I was just disappointed that it wasn't Amber. In retrospect, as an older, wiser (and more well-read) person, I find that to be a narrow opinion.<br/><br/>Yes, this book is definitely not Amber, but maybe that's for the best. We are spoiled with epic new fantasy now, but this clas</span>
  <span id="freeText12613721707177763285" style="display:none">Time to te-read some Roger Zelazny stuff. Though I re-read the Amber series periodically, I've been very lax about revisiting the other stuff of this top-tier fantastic author! 😯<br /><br />Post Re-read: I remember reading this AGES ago, and I was just disappointed that it wasn't Amber. In retrospect, as an older, wiser (and more well-read) person, I find that to be a narrow opinion.<br /><br />Yes, this book is definitely not Amber, but maybe that's for the best. We are spoiled with epic new fantasy now, but this classic nonetheless remains a taut, compelling read still. And, for a standalone book, there's quite a fair bit if depth to the setting. (Though that always was Zelaznys strong suit, IMO.)<br /><br />In short, not Amber, for better or worse. But it's still a hidden gem that deserves more attention than it gets.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10673661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4397417099593664550">2Aug2016 - currently rereading with the Sci-fi and Heroic Fantasy group here:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18195063'>https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br/><br/>This was one of the first Zelazny books I read & it's still fantastic. The characters aren't complex, but I think this is done on purpose. The only ones that much time is spent on are Dark Siders who have no soul. They're very uncomplicated, driven simply by desire, pride, & power. Jack personifies most & his thoughts are well documented. I thought his lame attempts at introspecti</span>
  <span id="freeText4397417099593664550" style="display:none">2Aug2016 - currently rereading with the Sci-fi and Heroic Fantasy group here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18195063">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br /><br />This was one of the first Zelazny books I read &amp; it's still fantastic. The characters aren't complex, but I think this is done on purpose. The only ones that much time is spent on are Dark Siders who have no soul. They're very uncomplicated, driven simply by desire, pride, &amp; power. Jack personifies most &amp; his thoughts are well documented. I thought his lame attempts at introspection were great. The few glimpses we get of those with souls are normal, complicated people. <br /><br />The last half was grim &amp; ugly, but hardly pointless, as Del Rey said. There were a couple of well setup up &amp; made points. The ending was fantastic.<br /><br /><br />7Dec09 - A very interesting fantasy/SF story. Jack, the hero, is an amoral, immortal whose self-interest leads further &amp; further into an interesting quest that ultimately changes the world. (MacBeth) Zelazny blends fantasy with SF until you're not quite sure which label applies. The story is told in his wonderfully concise style that makes re-reads a pleasure while the story haunts you in odd moments. Highly recommended.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13443689545377046994">A hard to find novel, but worth it if you can track it down. My copy fell apart long ago, and should I find a new one I'll grab it.<br/><br/>In a world frozen with a dark side and a light side (science predominates on the light side magic on the dark) one man functions in both worlds...<br/><br/>The dark side of this world is "ruled" or dominated by magic while the light side is dominated by science and technology.   <span id="freeText13443689545377046994" style="display:none">A hard to find novel, but worth it if you can track it down. My copy fell apart long ago, and should I find a new one I'll grab it.<br /><br />In a world frozen with a dark side and a light side (science predominates on the light side magic on the dark) one man functions in both worlds...<br /><br />The dark side of this world is "ruled" or dominated by magic while the light side is dominated by science and technology. The magic beings on the dark side are usually limited as the their power emanates from a location. Jack on the other hand is different. His power emanates or is drawn from shadow. While he is almost powerless in full light or full darkness access to any shadow makes him tremendously powerful. Due to his power he can function on both the dark magical side of the planet and the scientific light side.<br /><br />As noted I like the book. Some may find it a bit frustrating, though to say why may constitute a sort of spoiler. I do recommend it as it's a well written if short book.</span>

That and the writing style (which was just not for me) made me not really care for the characters because I couldn't really immerse myself into the story. The plot had</span>

The story jumped around quite a lot and sometimes I had to read a few pages of the chapter to even start to understand what was currently happening. That and the writing style (which was just not for me) made me not really care for the characters because I couldn't really immerse myself into the story. The plot had some amazing moments, and also some slower parts but the story itself was quite unique and well crafted.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer31154309&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer31154309" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer66053497980603586">Jack of Shadows, or Shadowjack, is a wizard and rogue, the best thief of his age. His world doesn't rotate. Instead, the light side is ruled by science and the dark side by magic. Daysiders have souls, Darksiders are eternally reborn in the Dung Pits of Glyve. Jack gets decapitated in the opening chapter and seeks revenge upon waking in the aforementioned Dung Pits. On the way to his goal, he gets imprisioned by an old enemy, spends time as a professor at a university on the Dayside, and finds K</span>
  <span id="freeText66053497980603586" style="display:none">Jack of Shadows, or Shadowjack, is a wizard and rogue, the best thief of his age. His world doesn't rotate. Instead, the light side is ruled by science and the dark side by magic. Daysiders have souls, Darksiders are eternally reborn in the Dung Pits of Glyve. Jack gets decapitated in the opening chapter and seeks revenge upon waking in the aforementioned Dung Pits. On the way to his goal, he gets imprisioned by an old enemy, spends time as a professor at a university on the Dayside, and finds Kolwria, the Key That Was Lost. Once he gets his revenge, a whole slew of other issues pop up.<br /><br />I found Jack of Shadows to be a very original work. Not a trace of the usual fantasy cliches. Philosophical questions like what it means to have a soul are raised. Jack reminded me of a magical version of the Rowan Atkinson Blackadder character. The ending is open for the reader to interpret.</span>

<div id="review_2493478368" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2493478368" />
    <a title="Rhys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1138007-rhys"><img alt="Rhys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442456315p2/1138007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2493478368?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhys" href="/user/show/1138007-rhys">Rhys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552096089" href="/book/show/1773785.Jack_of_Shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1138007-rhys?shelf=five-star-books">five-star-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2493478368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13795672541560720534">I read plenty of Zelazny when I was younger. In fact I have probably read most of his work. The one novel that eluded me for a long time was <i>Jack of Shadows</i>. This was doubly frustrating because I had heard it was his best book. Time passed and my enthusiasm for science fiction and fantasy began to wane somewhat. I haven't read any Zelazny for quite a while, but I always knew that if I ever managed to get hold of <i>Jack of Shadows</i> I would be eager to read it.<br/><br/>Finally last year I saw a second hand co</span>
  <span id="freeText13795672541560720534" style="display:none">I read plenty of Zelazny when I was younger. In fact I have probably read most of his work. The one novel that eluded me for a long time was <i>Jack of Shadows</i>. This was doubly frustrating because I had heard it was his best book. Time passed and my enthusiasm for science fiction and fantasy began to wane somewhat. I haven't read any Zelazny for quite a while, but I always knew that if I ever managed to get hold of <i>Jack of Shadows</i> I would be eager to read it.<br /><br />Finally last year I saw a second hand copy in a bookstore and bought it. Now I have read it. What do I think? It is very good indeed, and yes it is one of his best (maybe not quite the best of all). One of the amazing things about it is the coherent velocity of the action. The plot moves very fast and Zelazny throws in all sorts of twists and turns, yet the progression of the story doesn't feel as contrived as maybe it should. Zelazny's control is exquisite.<br /><br />Perhaps the greatest thing about this novel is the set-up of the world depicted. It is complex and original with plenty of potential for all the different elements to clash, combine and produce results that are difficult for the reader to predict. A non-rotating world held in stasis by a machine (or by fire elementals) and one that is prevented from freezing on one side and burning on the other by a cosmic shield that must be maintained with difficulty. The inhabitants of the dark side use magic; those of the light side use science. They are equal but opposite. There is also a twilight realm with people and cities. It is possible for one to be half darksider and half daysider.<br /><br />Jack of Shadows is a darksider but with a difference. Whereas most powerful darkside magicians are rooted in a place of power, in a particular location, Jack's power is contained in shadows -- any shadows cast anywhere -- and it is therefore mobile. He is thus free to wander, and in the grand tradition of the footloose wanderer he becomes a rogue, a masterful thief, but one with greater aspirations than normal. Indeed he has schemes that will change the societies of both sides forever.<br /><br />There is no need to say more. His journeys and the eccentric characters he meets and monsters he fights are remarkable. This novel was a delight to read. Of all the Zelazny novels I have read, only <i>Creatures of Light and Darkness</i> has pleased me more (a very lyrical novel that isn't the favourite of most readers, but which I adore).</span>
  <a data-text-id="13795672541560720534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_832167125" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/832167125" />
    <a title="Derek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1769635-derek"><img alt="Derek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232848809p2/1769635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/832167125?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Derek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Derek" href="/user/show/1769635-derek">Derek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0451135768" href="/book/show/9724105-jack-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769635-derek?shelf=appendix-n">appendix-n</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer832167125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2611763965610959124">I got it into my head that this was a "dying earth" style of book, in either homage to or imitation of Jack Vance, and found myself at odds with the style of writing and the way the story plays out. The finely-polished writing is minimalist in comparison, and while the darksiders live in a sort of civilized rivalry of false or real politeness, their language and interactions don't have the same sense of play or ornateness. I missed Vance's embellishment, and found that while there were moments o</span>
  <span id="freeText2611763965610959124" style="display:none">I got it into my head that this was a "dying earth" style of book, in either homage to or imitation of Jack Vance, and found myself at odds with the style of writing and the way the story plays out. The finely-polished writing is minimalist in comparison, and while the darksiders live in a sort of civilized rivalry of false or real politeness, their language and interactions don't have the same sense of play or ornateness. I missed Vance's embellishment, and found that while there were moments of real effectiveness--Jack imprisoned and dealing with the Lord of Bats, and Jack journeying the strangely populous underworld to the <i>Forbidden Planet</i>-style Great Machine at the center of it all--it simply didn't leap off the page.<br /><br />Where it lost its charm was the lightside, which by design or default is modeled after the 1960s, with references to punch cards, cigarettes, automobiles, and "computer time" as though using a centralized time-share system. Its sheer mundanity may be styled as a contrast to the mythical/legendary darkside, but I could not bridge the gap between the picture in my head and the supposed future-technology force fields that protect lightside from the unrelenting sun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2611763965610959124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2492123580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2492123580" />
    <a title="Greg Lemon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72343665-greg-lemon"><img alt="Greg Lemon" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2492123580?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg Lemon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg Lemon" href="/user/show/72343665-greg-lemon">Greg Lemon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2492123580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11273427281710372992">I am probably more at about three and a half stars for this one. I love Zelazny, my favorite sci fi author, but this is not one of his best in my opinion. It starts out well, Shadow Jack is an interesting character in an interesting world. But the last half kind of falls flat. Zelazny is at his best when his talented, witty protagonist (often pretty much the same guy from book to book, even fans will have to admit) is fighting the uphill battle as the cheeky upstart against the powers that be in</span>
  <span id="freeText11273427281710372992" style="display:none">I am probably more at about three and a half stars for this one. I love Zelazny, my favorite sci fi author, but this is not one of his best in my opinion. It starts out well, Shadow Jack is an interesting character in an interesting world. But the last half kind of falls flat. Zelazny is at his best when his talented, witty protagonist (often pretty much the same guy from book to book, even fans will have to admit) is fighting the uphill battle as the cheeky upstart against the powers that be in some very fantastic reality the author creates. In this book the battle is won too early, and the rest of the book falls just a little flatter, hence my lower rating. The ending is bit cheesy as well. <br /><br />I mentioned I re-read the book, probably for the 3-4th time, but it has been many years. The first part was pretty familiar and still enjoyable. The last half didn't leave enough of an impression on me to remember well. Yet even reading the 2nd half fresh and the first half familiar, I enjoyed the first half more. Still very much worth a read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11273427281710372992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer382161427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1003440241868417600"><br/>What a terrific read of science and magic. Roger Zelazny is the supreme master at mixing the two together. Roger Zelazny truly is fantastic at making someone despicable actually likeable. The Hero, more likely the anti-hero (it is up to you to choose) of the story, Jack is a character most would think to dislike, but simply for Zelazny work of masterful science/fantasy fiction, and in the first few chapters and especially at the end he makes you end up rooting for Jack, the <i>Jack of Shadows</i>! This</span>
  <span id="freeText1003440241868417600" style="display:none"><br />What a terrific read of science and magic. Roger Zelazny is the supreme master at mixing the two together. Roger Zelazny truly is fantastic at making someone despicable actually likeable. The Hero, more likely the anti-hero (it is up to you to choose) of the story, Jack is a character most would think to dislike, but simply for Zelazny work of masterful science/fantasy fiction, and in the first few chapters and especially at the end he makes you end up rooting for Jack, the <i>Jack of Shadows</i>! This is a book I plan on reading again. It is short and simple but also long and complex; in a good way that I don't understand how Zelazny does it, but he can condense a masterpiece in under 200 pages.<br /></span>

    <a title="Craig" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83180-craig"><img alt="Craig" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544792260p2/83180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2563297044?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Craig" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Craig" href="/user/show/83180-craig">Craig</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451135766" href="/book/show/1346120.Jack_of_Shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2563297044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3583675644392819568">This is one of Zelazny's shorter novels, and seems to be one that many readers either love or dislike immensely. While not as tautly-plotted as his myth-based Lord of Light or Creatures of Light and Darkness, I was mesmerized by the setting and the somewhat anti-hero characterization. I think Zelazny best examined his theme of science versus magic in this one, something he would return to again and again later in his career. I also loved his writing style, which was more ornate and lyrical than </span>
  <span id="freeText3583675644392819568" style="display:none">This is one of Zelazny's shorter novels, and seems to be one that many readers either love or dislike immensely. While not as tautly-plotted as his myth-based Lord of Light or Creatures of Light and Darkness, I was mesmerized by the setting and the somewhat anti-hero characterization. I think Zelazny best examined his theme of science versus magic in this one, something he would return to again and again later in his career. I also loved his writing style, which was more ornate and lyrical than in most of his more popular works. This is one of my favorites. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3583675644392819568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1599278478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1599278478" />
    <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc"><img alt="RJ from the LBC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605827139p2/131730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1599278478?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RJ from the LBC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RJ from the LBC" href="/user/show/131730-rj-from-the-lbc">RJ from the LBC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0451135768" href="/book/show/9724105-jack-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1599278478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15474532986788290803">Jack of Shadows is one of Roger Zelazny's earliest novels, although at the time of its publication the author was already well known and highly regarded in the SF/F industry for his Hugo Award winning novels This Immortal and Lord of Light. Jack of Shadows feels in many ways like a throwaway idea that Zelazny had while working on his Amber series (Nine Princes in Amber was published a year earlier) that he decided to work quickly into publishable form. Published first in 1971, the whole book ree</span>
  <span id="freeText15474532986788290803" style="display:none">Jack of Shadows is one of Roger Zelazny's earliest novels, although at the time of its publication the author was already well known and highly regarded in the SF/F industry for his Hugo Award winning novels This Immortal and Lord of Light. Jack of Shadows feels in many ways like a throwaway idea that Zelazny had while working on his Amber series (Nine Princes in Amber was published a year earlier) that he decided to work quickly into publishable form. Published first in 1971, the whole book reeks of the early 70s. Let's see, we've got our cigarette-smoking anti-hero (Jack), a disdain for societal niceties, marginalization and objectification of women, and a vague and unsatisfying ending which seemed to typify the era. But the book has flaws beyond just showing a little age. Jack of Shadows was said (per Wikipedia) to have been written in one draft, and the lack of polish shows. Characters are introduced and then quickly disposed of in various fashion with little to no dramatic flair since we never got to know them and could care less about them anyway. Some parts of the story have a lot of detail while other sections are way too vague. Not to say that everything about the book is bad - the world is very interesting, with half always in day and half always in night, populated with interesting lifeforms such as immortals, vampires and dragons to name a few. Zelazny's dialogue is terrific as always, like a SF/F Elmore Leonard. And it's these positive elements that actually make the book so frustrating because of the untapped potential that could have made the story so much more rewarding and entertaining. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15474532986788290803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6499761795755418915" style="display:none">Zelazny doing a Vance tribute? The only thing better would be <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5376.Jack_Vance" title="Jack Vance" rel="nofollow noopener">Jack Vance</a> doing a Zelazny tribute.<br /><br />In my more wistful moments, I like to imagine a world in which Jack Vance and Roger Zelazny were massively profitable authors with seven digit sales figures while <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks" title="Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Brooks</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan" title="Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan</a> were modestly successful but never crossed into the mainstream. I picture a world in which the industry standard is delivering an original setting, a compelling society, an intriguing main character, a complete plot arc, and one or two other ideas in less than 200 pages, while pooping out 500+ pages of halfassed Tokienisms would be considered lazy and pointless. That's the world I wish I lived in.</span>

  <span id="freeText5187096295655737168" style="display:none">The nightside thief Jack of Shadows is killed for merely contemplating a theft, but those from the nightside have multiple lives and a thirst for vengeance...<br /><br />The main character is not particularly likable and as a tale of revenge it's fairly good but it's no Hamlet. The thing with even Zelazny's lesser works is he had an incredible talent for writing mythologically. You can feel the other stories spinning off from a person or a place mentioned in this one, perhaps with a vague sense that those stories must have been burned with the Library of Alexandria or else surely we would have heard of them.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1169193676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10001331307995336484">Literally couldn't say enough about this book. I read it every so often and as short as it is it packs a lot in there. Jack is one of my favorite characters out of all the books I've read. I most enjoy the fact that for the most part he uses his powers for good but at times he abuses them as well if he feels necessary. All around just a great story and I'd recommend to anyone who reads sci-fi or anything to do with magic as well.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2431581008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3818766913947136802">Storyline: 3/5<br/>Characters: 2/5<br/>Writing Style: 2/5<br/>World: 3/5<br/><br/>I always look forward to reading Zelazny. I never seem to regret finishing his stories even though I rarely enjoy them all the way through. He's one of the more creative and versatile fantasy/sc fi writers I've come across, and this picaresque fantasy was everything I expected it to be. "Slapdash" carries with it the connotation of carelessness but more specifically refers to the haphazard character of a work. I'm convinced that slapdash c</span>
  <span id="freeText3818766913947136802" style="display:none">Storyline: 3/5<br />Characters: 2/5<br />Writing Style: 2/5<br />World: 3/5<br /><br />I always look forward to reading Zelazny. I never seem to regret finishing his stories even though I rarely enjoy them all the way through. He's one of the more creative and versatile fantasy/sc fi writers I've come across, and this picaresque fantasy was everything I expected it to be. "Slapdash" carries with it the connotation of carelessness but more specifically refers to the haphazard character of a work. I'm convinced that slapdash can be perfected; that worlds with inexplicable boundaries, undeveloped characters, unexplained powers, and offbeat continuity can be transformed from their disparate and fragmentary pieces into a much greater whole. Jack of Shadows had no such ambitions, however. Some of the pieces are there: there's a rakish protagonist with bizarre and enigmatic abilities. There's a world that is like ours, twisted, however, with bits of myth and legend into something very different. There's a teasing blend of science and magic that is as incomprehensible to the characters as it is to the reader. Each piece is a scene, though, never carefully weighed or placed. In a perfected slapdash what is left unexplained and incongruous should add to the tale. Here the impression throughout is of a hurried draft from a talented author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3818766913947136802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1714377255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1714377255" />
    <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley"><img alt="Pam Baddeley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442488147p2/42764850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1714377255?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam Baddeley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam Baddeley" href="/user/show/42764850-pam-baddeley">Pam Baddeley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552096089" href="/book/show/1773785.Jack_of_Shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42764850-pam-baddeley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1714377255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7565612292415468195">This was a re-read of a book that I remember loving when I read it years ago as a teenager. Unfortunately, it hasn't really stood the test of time, and maybe I'm a more critical reader too.<br/><br/>The beginning is great - Zelazny makes no attempt to set the scene - we are just dumped into a situation and have to make sense of it as the story goes along. The anti-hero Jack also known as Jack of Shadows or Shadowjack is a long lived being from the dark side of the planet who has been caught hanging around</span>
  <span id="freeText7565612292415468195" style="display:none">This was a re-read of a book that I remember loving when I read it years ago as a teenager. Unfortunately, it hasn't really stood the test of time, and maybe I'm a more critical reader too.<br /><br />The beginning is great - Zelazny makes no attempt to set the scene - we are just dumped into a situation and have to make sense of it as the story goes along. The anti-hero Jack also known as Jack of Shadows or Shadowjack is a long lived being from the dark side of the planet who has been caught hanging around with intent at a games where a fabulous gem is on offer as prize. He is denounced to the organiser by two contestants and the organiser has him executed immediately, solely on the basis of his reputation as thief. The contestants work for one of the Powers who rule darkside: the Lord of Bats. By the end of chapter one, Jack is resigned to his beheading, but vows that he will come back - though from a ghastly place called the Dungpits of Glyve - and will wreck vengeance on his list of enemies which includes the two contestants, the executioner, the games organiser and the Lord of Bats himself.<br /><br />Next, Jack wakes up in the pits and has to regain his senses and travel back through great dangers, showing resourcefulness and also an amoral lack of compassion or sensitivity, possibly because all darksiders lack souls. Only the light siders who have only one life believe they have souls. So Jack's response to a beautiful singing bird is to eat it as a snack.<br /><br />Eventually Jack's vengeance quest takes him to the light side of the planet where a society very similar to early 1970s USA (the book was published in 1971) exists, including the type of vast computer where you had to book time to run a program. And Jack takes up smoking which he proceeds to do a lot. <br /><br />I won't say whether Jack achieves his vengeance or lives to gain a type of morality and to regret his deeds. The main problem with the book despite its inventiveness - and I do love the idea of someone who can take strength from shadows - is that there is no real development of the characters and some are just ciphers so that it isn't possible to feel any sympathy for them. Jack is developed more, but given his casual cruelties doesn't engage this reader at least. So although I like some aspects, the book doesn't live up to my memory of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7565612292415468195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2022632182" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rindis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rindis" href="/user/show/145461-rindis">Rindis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30125143-jack-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/145461-rindis?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/145461-rindis?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2022632182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14329872865495181001">I’ve found that the best way to sum up this book is, “It’s a Roger Zelazny novel.”<br/><br/>For anyone who doesn’t really know what that means, I’ll try to explain.<br/><br/>With a world where one half is perpetually day, and the other is night, the populations of both are similarly segregated. Daytime has normal humans and a technological civilization, and nighttime has sorcerers who come back from the dead an unspecified number of times. Magic and technology only work their respective halves of the world, and onl</span>
  <span id="freeText14329872865495181001" style="display:none">I’ve found that the best way to sum up this book is, “It’s a Roger Zelazny novel.”<br /><br />For anyone who doesn’t really know what that means, I’ll try to explain.<br /><br />With a world where one half is perpetually day, and the other is night, the populations of both are similarly segregated. Daytime has normal humans and a technological civilization, and nighttime has sorcerers who come back from the dead an unspecified number of times. Magic and technology only work their respective halves of the world, and only mix in the twilight area. There’s some philosophical discussions of looking at the world in different ways, but mostly this is just allowed to make the novel something of a mish-mash, with parts fantasy, and modern day academia.<br /><br />There’s a secondary-character subplot that never quite comes into it’s own, along with a few more that do. And after wandering around a bit, there’s an epic-scale ending.<br /><br />And despite the way all that sounds, it works. It’s not great (and is not one of his best works), but just about everything in the novel ties back into his main themes. It doesn’t really come to any solid conclusions, and you could say the same of the action, though things are definitely finished.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14329872865495181001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2078456649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2078456649" />

        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/52388598-richard">Richard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7177570-jack-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52388598-richard?shelf=trash">trash</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52388598-richard?shelf=vintage-sff">vintage-sff</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2078456649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15928598443579588292">The setting is reminiscent of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5376.Jack_Vance' title='Jack Vance' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jack Vance</a>'s Dying Earth. Although, initially, I got a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12728.Darrell_Schweitzer' title='Darrell Schweitzer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darrell Schweitzer</a> vibe from the characters and settings. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/23113.John_Brunner' title='John Brunner' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Brunner</a>'s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41083.The_Traveller_in_Black' title='The Traveller in Black by John Brunner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Traveller in Black</a> also comes to mind. This holds true for the first part of the story. The second part, well, it was jarring with the stark difference in settings. Going in I imagined that if the dark half of the world was archaic and magic worked then the light side of the world would be the pinnacle of science. This was not so. The l</span>
  <span id="freeText15928598443579588292" style="display:none">The setting is reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5376.Jack_Vance" title="Jack Vance" rel="nofollow noopener">Jack Vance</a>'s Dying Earth. Although, initially, I got a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12728.Darrell_Schweitzer" title="Darrell Schweitzer" rel="nofollow noopener">Darrell Schweitzer</a> vibe from the characters and settings. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/23113.John_Brunner" title="John Brunner" rel="nofollow noopener">John Brunner</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41083.The_Traveller_in_Black" title="The Traveller in Black by John Brunner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Traveller in Black</a> also comes to mind. This holds true for the first part of the story. The second part, well, it was jarring with the stark difference in settings. Going in I imagined that if the dark half of the world was archaic and magic worked then the light side of the world would be the pinnacle of science. This was not so. The light side of the world was mundane, ordinary, nothing to differentiate it from today. This did not sit well with my preconceptions of the story. Finally I wasn't a fan of the ambiguous ending either. So, with as much as I wanted to like it and with as much as I liked the beginning, this one just didn't make the cut. It's going on the discard pile.</span>

    <a title="Haaze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6941528-haaze"><img alt="Haaze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591937826p2/6941528.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haaze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haaze" href="/user/show/6941528-haaze">Haaze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0451135768" href="/book/show/9724105-jack-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Zelazny as well as high fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6941528-haaze?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236794267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7528100725366814154">This was a book that mesmerized me as a teenager and was a pathway into fantasy and science fiction. Reading it now years later I find myself much more critical. Zelazny had an amazing imagination as he created a world where one side is in the dark and the other is in light with a twilight zone in-between. Magic rules on the dark side and science on the other. He focuses on Jack of Shadows as the main character which gains his power from shadow. Regardless, as a reader we follow the many adventu</span>
  <span id="freeText7528100725366814154" style="display:none">This was a book that mesmerized me as a teenager and was a pathway into fantasy and science fiction. Reading it now years later I find myself much more critical. Zelazny had an amazing imagination as he created a world where one side is in the dark and the other is in light with a twilight zone in-between. Magic rules on the dark side and science on the other. He focuses on Jack of Shadows as the main character which gains his power from shadow. Regardless, as a reader we follow the many adventures facing Jack as he moves through his world. My memory of the book was as one of the greatest fantasy books ever written. Today I cannot really agree with my teenage mind. The book feels somewhat rough and undeveloped with plenty of dead ends even though it is crammed with great ideas. His writing is also highly variable ranging from crude and simplistic to poetic and very descriptive. It is almost as if Zelazny moved through different frames of mind when he was writing the book. Still, a classic in the realm of fantasy books and well worth reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7528100725366814154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1620644272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1620644272" />
    <a title="HBalikov" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/929238-hbalikov"><img alt="HBalikov" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271764879p2/929238.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1620644272?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HBalikov" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HBalikov" href="/user/show/929238-hbalikov">HBalikov</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1620644272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8423486002859502369">No, this isn’t the Earth you are familiar with. Yes, humans still are the dominant species. Yes, the birds and animals are present. But, this planet shows only one face continually to the Sun. One side always in bright light and the other in perpetual night, which might have some interesting effects on evolution. Because this is Zelazny, we get to know a bit of why one side doesn’t have just boiling rock and the other side a frozen environment where nothing moves. This world is protected by a “…</span>
  <span id="freeText8423486002859502369" style="display:none">No, this isn’t the Earth you are familiar with. Yes, humans still are the dominant species. Yes, the birds and animals are present. But, this planet shows only one face continually to the Sun. One side always in bright light and the other in perpetual night, which might have some interesting effects on evolution. Because this is Zelazny, we get to know a bit of why one side doesn’t have just boiling rock and the other side a frozen environment where nothing moves. This world is protected by a “…spell-wrought Shield (that) kept the darkside from freezing into Allwinter as surely as their force screens prevented the daysiders from frying in the merciless glare of the sun.” Between these extremes, there exists a narrow belt of twilight, and there is Jack of Shadows. <br />It is not long after we are introduced to Jack that we see him captured (betrayed by the Lord of Bats?) and executed. He begins his next life on a mound of offal in a lake of filth in the dominion of Lord Dreckheim. <br /> <br />It suited Zelazny’s zeitgeist to have Jack be a lord, the Lord of Shadows. [If you are interested in a more extensive exploration of the elements of fealty and vassalage, Zelazny’s Chronicles of Amber, begun at about the same time, extends for a vast number of novels and takes up some similar themes including the nature of shadow.] Yet, here, the shadow lord is in great peril and, as we come to know him, we note elements of his nature and moral code emerging.<br /><br />“He felt a kiss upon his throat and the alb of her long hair that lay on his shoulders.<br />“For a long moment he rested there, trying to muster his remaining strength (difficult to locate food or drink in this land, without being caught). He seized her hair with his left hand, as his right are moved about her body. Forcing her away from him, he rolled to his left, knowing from his waking instant what must be done. With just a fraction of his old speed, his head dropped forward.<br />“When he had finished, he wiped his mouth, stood and stared down at the limp form.<br />“’Poor vampire,’ he said. ‘There was not much blood in you which is why you wanted mine so desperately, yet were so weak in its taking. But I, too, was desperate in my hunger. We do what we must.’<br />“Wearing the black skirts, cloak and tight-fitting boots he had appropriated, Jack moved…Climbing, circling, sometimes running, his hatred grew more rapidly than the hunger within him….One by one he would seek them and have his revenge upon them…he thought in terms of torture rather than a simple sword thrust. They had hurt his feeling by killing him in this manner. Had they done it differently, he might have been less aggrieved.”<br /><br />And there is the desired Evene, daughter of the Colonel Who Never Died. Jack is dead because the Colonel demanded the Hellflame as a bride price for his daughter. So, it seems, Jack must still steal the Hellflame if he and Evene are to be united.<br /><br />Zelazny has often demonstrated his command of both myth and action. It is a rare story he has written that doesn’t plunge ahead from one element of adventure to the next. Jack of Shadows is certainly no exception.<br /><br />However, the masterful mixing of those components is what sets this ahead of many of his other works. It is hard to discern whether this is a story of past or future Earth (if Earth at all). Is Jack more like the Norse Loki or the Greek Prometheus? Is his flaw his desire for revenge or his temptation for power? Was he channeling Matthew: <br />“For what doth it profit a man, if he gain the whole world, and suffer the loss of his own soul?”<br />Or Mark: “For what shall it profit a man, if he shall gain the whole world, and lose his own soul?”<br /><br />Because that is where this story leads, with Jack’s soul tagging behind as a world so cleverly divided between light and darkness breaks apart. Take the ride, and discover if Jack ever allows himself to appreciate what is around him. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8423486002859502369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_285290969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285290969" />
    <a title="Alazzar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3531937-alazzar"><img alt="Alazzar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328030890p2/3531937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/285290969?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alazzar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alazzar" href="/user/show/3531937-alazzar">Alazzar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285290969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15553926510552182560">I love a good revenge story.<br/><br/>That might explain why I love Roger Zelazny so much.<br/><br/>When Zelazny’s characters are treated poorly, they will stop at <i>nothing</i> to see the offending party punished. And I don’t mean this in an “eye for an eye” sort of way. If you take a Zelazny character’s eye, you can plan on losing a whole lot more than that when he comes looking for you, because his plan for revenge will far exceed whatever the original offense was.<br/><br/>Jack of Shadows (the man, not the book) is no exceptio</span>
  <span id="freeText15553926510552182560" style="display:none">I love a good revenge story.<br /><br />That might explain why I love Roger Zelazny so much.<br /><br />When Zelazny’s characters are treated poorly, they will stop at <i>nothing</i> to see the offending party punished. And I don’t mean this in an “eye for an eye” sort of way. If you take a Zelazny character’s eye, you can plan on losing a whole lot more than that when he comes looking for you, because his plan for revenge will far exceed whatever the original offense was.<br /><br />Jack of Shadows (the man, not the book) is no exception to this rule.<br /><br />Revenge stories, for the most part, follow a formula: dude is treated like crap, dude gets angry, dude comes up with a plan to avenge himself, dude makes plan happen (or dies trying). <i>Fin.</i> So what makes <i>Jack of Shadows</i> (the book, not the man) unique? What makes it worthy of five stars?<br /><br />I don’t know, it could be Zelazny’s voice, which always gets bonus points from me. But that alone is not enough for five stars—after all, I’ve given some of his works a lowly <i>three</i>. Maybe this book’s rating has more to do with its unique magic system (all darksider lords have power attached to a certain geographical location, save for Jack, who draws his power from shadows). Or maybe it’s the laws of the world Zelazny has created (the story takes place on a planet which never rotates, leaving one side forever in the sun’s light and the other shrouded in darkness). Or <i>maybe</i> it’s the fact that Zelazny once again mixed science with magic, creating a scenario where one half of the world follows the laws of science and the other serves magic.<br /><br />It could also have something to do with the fact that Zelazny packs more imagination into 200 pages than most authors do in twice that much.<br /><br />Or it could be something else entirely. Who knows?<br /><br />In any case, I loved <i>Jack of Shadows,</i> even though I haven’t read the full novel. My library and local bookstore didn’t have a copy of the book, so I ended up reading the abridged version that was originally serialized in <i>The Magazine of Fantasy &amp; Science Fiction</i> in 1971 (because I just so happen to own those issues, for some reason). I have no idea how much my version differs from the novel, but I’ll say this: my version smells awesome. It’s just very clearly <i>old</i>. Love it.<br /><br />Anyway, this book was published during Zelazny’s prime, and it shows. If you’re looking for a good quick read (and don’t mind an anti-hero who can be downright despicable at times), give <i>Jack of Shadows</i> a shot. You won’t regret it! Or maybe you will. But that’s not my problem. So, <i>whatever.</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15553926510552182560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
